 </div<br><br>        </aside<br>          </div<br>    <div class="desktop:grid-col-12"<br>        <div id="block-usgs-tantalum-content" class="block block-system block-system-main-block"<br>  <br>    <br>      <br>  <br>  <div class="node-top grid-container node--type--science"<br>    <br>          <h1<br>          Specific Heat Capacity and Water<br><br>                  <span class="science-status"  Completed<br></span<br>              </h1<br>                      <div class="owner-date"<br>      <span class="by-line"<br>      By <a href="/special-topics/water-science-school" hreflang="en"Water Science School</a<br>    </span<br>        <span class="date"<br>      June 6, 2018<br>    </span<br>  </div      </div<br><br><br>  <div class="carousel "<br>      <br>  <br><br><div class="usgs-carousel slick-initialized slick-slider" data-once="usgs-carousel"<br>      <br><br><br>        <br>  <div class="slick-list draggable"<div class="slick-track" style="opacity: 1; width: 611px; transform: translate3d(0px, 0px, 0px);"<div class="paragraph--type--carousel-item slick-slide slick-current slick-active" style="background: url(&quot;https://d9-wret.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/assets/palladium/production/s3fs-public/styles/carousel/public/thumbnails/image/wss-banner-property-heat-capacity.jpg?itok=dcb9Txih&quot;) 50% 50% / cover no-repeat; width: 611px;" aria-label="" data-slick-index="0" aria-hidden="false" tabindex="0"<br>    <br>      <div class="grid-container carousel-content-wrapper"<br>        <div class="carousel-content widescreen:grid-offset-3 widescreen:grid-col-7 desktop:grid-offset-1 desktop:grid-col-9 tablet:grid-offset-1 tablet:grid-col-9 mobile-lg:grid-col-10"<br><br>          <div class="usgs-breadcrumbs__list"<br>            <div class="usgs-breadcrumbs__list-item"<br>              <br>            </div<br>          </div<br><br>                                        <br>        </div<br>              </div<br>      </div</div</div<br><br>  </div<br><br><br><br>  <br><br>  </div<br><br><div class="clearfix"</div<br><br><div class="grid-container"<br>  <div about="/special-topics/water-science-school/science/specific-heat-capacity-and-water" class="node node--type--science node--view-mode--full grid-row grid-gap-3"<br>    <br>    <div class="desktop:grid-col-12"<br>      <div class="grid-row grid-gap-3"<br>        <div class="node-intro desktop:grid-col-12"<br>                    <br>                              <br>          <br>        </div<br><br>        <br>        <div class="node-main desktop:grid-col-12' }} "<br><br>          <br>          <br>          <div class="usgs-tabs-wrapper related-content related-info ui-tabs ui-corner-all ui-widget ui-widget-content" data-once="usgs-tabs-wrapper"<br>    <ul class="usgs-tabs related-content-tabs-desktop ui-tabs-nav ui-corner-all ui-helper-reset ui-helper-clearfix ui-widget-header" role="tablist"<br>                  <li role="tab" tabindex="0" class="ui-tabs-tab ui-corner-top ui-state-default ui-tab ui-tabs-active ui-state-active" aria-controls="overview" aria-labelledby="ui-id-1" aria-selected="true" aria-expanded="true"<br>          <a href="#overview" tabindex="-1" class="ui-tabs-anchor" id="ui-id-1"<br>            Overview<br>          </a<br>        </li<br>                        <li role="tab" tabindex="-1" class="ui-tabs-tab ui-corner-top ui-state-default ui-tab" aria-controls="science" aria-labelledby="ui-id-2" aria-selected="false" aria-expanded="false"<br>          <a href="#science" tabindex="-1" class="ui-tabs-anchor" id="ui-id-2"<br>            Science<br>          </a<br>        </li<br>                        <li role="tab" tabindex="-1" class="ui-tabs-tab ui-corner-top ui-state-default ui-tab" aria-controls="multimedia" aria-labelledby="ui-id-3" aria-selected="false" aria-expanded="false"<br>          <a href="#multimedia" tabindex="-1" class="ui-tabs-anchor" id="ui-id-3"<br>            Multimedia<br>          </a<br>        </li<br>            </ul<br>  <div class="usgs-tabs-main"<br>                  <div class="usgs-tabs-content tab ui-tabs-panel ui-corner-bottom ui-widget-content" id="overview" aria-labelledby="ui-id-1" role="tabpanel" aria-hidden="false"<br>          <br>  <br><br><div about="/special-topics/water-science-school/science/specific-heat-capacity-and-water" class="node node--type--science node--view-mode--overview grid-row grid-gap-3"<br><br>  <div class="node-main desktop:grid-col-9"<br><br>          <br><div class="intro-cta"<br>      <br><div class="field field--name--field-intro field--type--text-long field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="field-intro"<pWater has a high specific heat capacity—it absorbs a lot of heat before it begins to get hot. You may not know how that affects you, but the specific heat of water has a huge role to play in the Earth's climate and helps determine the habitability of many places around the globe.</p</div<br>  <br></div<br><br>  </div<br><br><div class="field field--name--field-content field--type--entity-reference-revisions field--label--hidden"<br>  <br>          <div class="field-content field-loop-count-1 field-first field-last"  <div class="paragraph paragraph--type--wysiwyg-text-with-media paragraph--view-mode--default"<br>          <br><div class="field field--name--field-text-with-media field--type--text-long field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="field-text-with-media"<div class="tex2jax_process"<p<strong•&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="/special-topic/water-science-school"Water Science School HOME</a&nbsp;&nbsp;•&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="/special-topic/water-science-school/science/water-properties-0"Water Properties topics</a&nbsp; •</strong</p<br><p&nbsp;</p<br><figure role="group" class="align-right side-image"<br><br>  <div class="d-media embedded-media d-media--type--image media--view-mode--side-image"<br>          <a href="/media/images/mild-climate-scilly-england-partly-due-heat-capacity"<br>            <br><div class="field field--name--image field--type--image field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="image"  <img loading="lazy" src="https://d9-wret.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/assets/palladium/production/s3fs-public/styles/side_image/public/thumbnails/image/wss-property-heat-capacity-beach.jpg?itok=3Ys0fRTP" width="340" height="231" alt="A beach in Scilly, England, showing tropical plants" typeof="foaf:Image"<br><br><br></div<br>  <br></div<br><br>          </a<br>              <div class="d-media-copyright"<br>        Sources/Usage: Some content may have restrictions. <a href="/media/images/mild-climate-scilly-england-partly-due-heat-capacity"View Media Details</a<br>      </div<br>          </div<br><br><figcaptionThe specific heat of water is partially responsible for the mild climate along Englands southwestern shore. There are beaches, as at Porthcressa Beach in Scilly, where tropical plants grow.<br<br><br<br>Credit: Wikimedia</figcaption<br></figure<br><pSpecific heat is defined by the amount of heat needed to raise the temperature of 1 gram of a substance 1 degree Celsius (°C).&nbsp;Water has a high specific heat,&nbsp;meaning it takes more energy&nbsp;to increase the temperature of water compared to other substances. This is why water is valuable to industries and in your car's radiator as a coolant. The high specific heat of water also helps regulate the rate at which air changes temperature, which is why the temperature change between seasons is gradual rather than sudden, especially near the oceans.</p<br><pThis same concept can be expanded to a world-wide scale. The oceans and lakes help regulate the temperature ranges that billions of people experience in their towns and cities. Water surrounding or near cities take longer to heat up and longer to cool down than do land masses, so cities near the oceans will tend to have less change and less extreme temperatures than inland cities. This property of water is one reason why states on the coast and in the center of the United States can differ so much in temperature patterns. A Midwest state, such as Nebraska, will have colder winters and hotter summers than Oregon, which has a higher latitude but has the Pacific Ocean nearby.</p<br><pIf you leave a bucket of water outside in the sun in summer it will certainly get warm, but not hot enough to boil an egg. But, if you walk barefoot on the black asphalt of a street in the southern portion of the United States&nbsp;in August, you'll burn your feet. Dropping an egg on the metal of my car hood on an August day will produce a fried egg. Metals have a much lower specific heat&nbsp;than water. If you've ever held onto a needle and put the other end in a flame you know how fast the needle gets hot, and how fast the heat is moved through the length of the needle to your finger. Not so with water.</p<br><p&nbsp;</p<br><h3Why heat capacity is important</h3<br><figure role="group" class="align-left side-image"<br><br>  <div class="d-media embedded-media d-media--type--image media--view-mode--side-image"<br>          <a href="/media/images/waters-high-specific-heat-capacity-ideal-pond"<br>            <br><div class="field field--name--image field--type--image field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="image"  <img loading="lazy" src="https://d9-wret.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/assets/palladium/production/s3fs-public/styles/side_image/public/thumbnails/image/wss-property-heat-capacity-pond.jpg?itok=-9nZ7u9G" width="340" height="231" alt="Fish pond" typeof="foaf:Image"<br><br><br></div<br>  <br></div<br><br>          </a<br>              <div class="d-media-copyright"<br>        Sources/Usage: Some content may have restrictions. <a href="/media/images/waters-high-specific-heat-capacity-ideal-pond"View Media Details</a<br>      </div<br>          </div<br><br><figcaptionCredit: LENA15 | pixabay.com</figcaption<br></figure<br><pThe high specific heat of water has a great deal to do with regulating extremes in the environment. For instance, the fish in this pond&nbsp;are happy because the specific heat of the water in the pond means the temperature of the water will stay relatively the same from day to night. They don't have to worry about either turning on the air conditioner or putting on their woolen flipper gloves.&nbsp;(Also, for happy fish, check out our page on <strong<a href="/special-topic/water-science-school/science/dissolved-oxygen-and-water"Dissolved Oxygen</a</strong.)</p<br><pLucky for me, you, and the fish in the pond to the right, water has a higher specific heat than many other substances. One of water's most significant properties is that it takes a lot of energy to heat it. Precisely, water has to absorb 4,184 Joules of heat (1 kilocalorie) for the temperature of one kilogram of water to increase 1°C. For comparison sake, it only takes 385 Joules of heat to raise 1 kilogram of copper 1°C.</p<br><pIf you'd like to learn more about the specific heat of water at the molecular level, check out this video on the <a href="https://www.khanacademy.org/science/biology/water-acids-and-bases/water-as-a-solid-liquid-and-gas/v/specific-heat-of-water" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer"specific heat&nbsp;of water</a from Khan Academy.</p<br></div</div<br>  <br></div<br><br>      </div<br></div<br>  <br></div<br><br>        <br>    <br>  </div<br><br>      <aside class="p-usgs-sidebar node-sidebar desktop:grid-col-3"<br>      <br><div class="sidebar-block sidebar-map-thumbnail"<h3Study Area</h3<a class="modal-popup-link" data-link="/sidebar-map/node/44004"<img alt="Map Thumbnail" src="https://d9-wret.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/assets/palladium/production/s3fs-public/geodata/thumbnails/node-44004.jpg?time=1712928812"</a</div<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>    <div class="sidebar-block c-usgs-explore-science"<br>    <h3Explore Search</h3<br>    <ul class="usa-list--unstyled"<li<a href="/search?keywords=Physical Water Properties"Physical Water Water Properties Information by Topic<br><br>              </a<br>          </h4<br>    <br><div class="field field--name--field-intro field--type--text-long field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="field-intro"  Looking at water, you might think that it's the most simple thing around. Pure water is practically colorless, odorless, and tasteless. But it's not at all simple and plain and it is vital for all life on Earth. Where there is water there is life, and where water is scarce, life has to struggle or just "throw in the towel." Continue on to learn about dozens of water properties.<br><br></div<br>  <br></div<br><br>        <br>    <br>    <br>    <br>  </div<br></div<br></div<br><br><br><br>  <br><div class="science-mobile"<br><div class="contextual-region node node--type--science node--view-mode--teaser c-usgs-teaser"<br>  <div class="d-image" style="background: linear-gradient(to bottom, rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.4), rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.4)), url('https://d9-wret.s3.us-west-2.amazonaws.com/assets/palladium/production/s3fs-public/styles/teaser/public/thumbnails/image/water_prop_banner.png?itok=gPZBVl2m') 50% 50% no-repeat; background-size: cover;"<br>    <a href="/special-topics/water-science-school/science/water-properties-information-topic" class="d-link"<span class="usa-sr-only"link</span</a<br>    <div class="d-title-info"<br>      <div class="d-info"  <time datetime="2019-10-22T05:00:00Z"October 22, 2019</time<br><br></div<br>      <h4 class="d-title" style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"  Water Properties Information by Topic<br></h4<br>    </div<br>  </div<br>  <div class="d-teaser-body"<br>    <br><div class="field field--name--field-intro field--type--text-long field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="field-intro"  Looking at water, you might think that it's the most simple thing around. Pure water is practically colorless, odorless, and tasteless. But it's not at all simple and plain and it is vital for all life on Earth. Where there is water there is life, and where water is scarce, life has to struggle or just "throw in the towel." href="/special-topics/water-science-school/science/temperature-and-water"<br>                Temperature and Water<br><br>              </a<br>          </h4<br>    <br><div class="field field--name--field-intro field--type--text-long field--label--hidden"<br>    <br>      <div class="field-intro"  Water temperature plays an important role in almost all USGS water science. Water temperature exerts a major influence on biological activity and growth, has an effect on water chemistry, can influence water quantity measurements, and governs the kinds of organisms that live in water bodies.<br><br></div<br>  <br></div<br><br>        <br>    <br>    <br>    <br><div class="field field--name--field-attributions field--type--computed-string-long field--label--inline"<br>      <div class="field-label"By</div<br>    <br>      <div class="field-attributions"<span class="attribution"<a href="/mission-areas/water-resources" hreflang="en"Water Resources Mission Area</a, </span<span class="attribution"<a href="/special-topics/water-science-school" hreflang="en"Water Science School</a</span</div<br>  <br></div

data-component="LayoutContainer"<div<div<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Right now, people in coastal China are fleeing successive typhoons. Parts of the Philippines are awash.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Typhoons are intense circular storms, which Australians know as tropical cyclones and Americans call hurricanes. Damage from cyclones has increased sevenfold since the 1980s, even as death tolls fell dramatically. In the 2010s, tropical cyclones did $872 billion worth of damage globally.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Why? Our world has more heat in the oceans and atmosphere, which can supercharge cyclones. A cyclone is a heat engine, transferring heat from warm ocean water up into colder layers of the atmosphere. More heat in the system means more intense heat engines.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"No wonder there's been renewed interest in Cold War era experiments in weather control. While early efforts had little success, our new research evaluates other methods of weakening these storms by pumping up cold water from the depths or spreading particles in the lower atmosphere to reduce incoming heat and encourage early rainfall.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"But these techniques could have unexpected – or even dangerous – side effects.</p<div aria-label="Social media embed" class="ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_outdentDesktop__ijbiK" data-print="inline-media" itemid="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=el7aoPUcaCo" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/SocialMediaPosting"<figure class="Figure_figure__NnqTc" role="group" data-print="inline-media" aria-labelledby="abc-:r1:" data-component="Social"<div class="AspectRatio_container__FC_XH" data-component="AspectRatioContainer" style="--aspect-ratio: 1.7777777777777777;"<div class="Social_embed__C3Ljn"<div<div<iframe width="200" height="113" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/el7aoPUcaCo?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" allowfullscreen="" title="As floodwaters recede, China’s northern cities faces 'bitter' days ahead | The World"</iframe</div</div</div</div<figcaption class="Typography_base__sj2RP Figure_figcaption___vGe0 Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile20___U7Vr Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" id="abc-:r1:" data-component="Figure__figcaption"<span class="Figure_prefix__GumH0"YouTube</span As floodwaters recede, China’s northern cities faces 'bitter' days ahead.</figcaption</figure</div<h2 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B Typography_sizeMobile20__NUDn4 Typography_sizeDesktop32__LR_G6 Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop40__BuoRf Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="Heading"Why are researchers even looking into this?</h2<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Tropical cyclones are lethal. In 1970, an enormous cyclone struck Bangladesh (then East Pakistan). Meteorologists knew it was coming, but they had no way to communicate to people in its path. The storm killed up to 500,000 people.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Since then, we've invested in far better early warning systems. Deaths have fallen substantially now that people have time to evacuate.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"But in developing countries in particular, deaths still happen. And then there's the damage to farms, houses, roads and livestock. You may well survive the storm only to be forced into poverty.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Scientists are exploring ways of preventing natural disasters, from bushfires to floods to hailstorms. So why not cyclones?</p<figure class="ArticleFigure_content__ueJhz ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_outdentDesktop__ijbiK ArticleFigure_outdent__tkMFK" role="group" data-component="ArticleFigure" aria-labelledby="102706256" data-uri="coremedia://imageproxy/102706256"<img alt="Two woman share a canoe in a flooded street. with a 7/11 store behind them. loading="lazy" data-component="Image" style="--ratio-width:3;--ratio-height:2" data-lazy="true"<div class="ArticleFigcaption_desktopCaption__HYT8t"<figcaption class="Typography_base__sj2RP year.<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP ArticleFigcaption_citation__5osFt Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx class="ArticleFigcaption_caption__PDo_T"<button class="Button_btn___qFSk ArticleFigcaption_button__xUfr_ Button_filled__Z0XIL Button_uppercase__u_om3 Button_hasIcon__G3VLB Button_iconOnly__q0bR0" aria-label="Show caption" data-component="Button" aria-expanded="false" type="button"<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-component="Info" class="icon_icon__9kCSO icon_size24__GkyQ9"<circle cx="12" cy="12" r="9" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2"</circle<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="M12 7v2m0 2v6"</path</svg</button</div</figure<h2 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B Typography_sizeMobile20__NUDn4 Typography_sizeDesktop32__LR_G6 Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop40__BuoRf Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="Heading"Can we really turn a cyclone into a normal storm?</h2<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"It is certainly possible. But it's not easy.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"In the 1960s, the United States explored the use of cloud seeding to stop hurricanes from forming.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"During Project STORMFURY, planes flew high above cyclones out at sea and sprayed them with silver iodide, a chemical which could encourage water droplets to clump together and fall as rain. This, the theory ran, would disrupt the hurricane from forming. While some seedings seemed to correlate with weaker hurricanes, the link was never adequately found and the project was eventually abandoned.</p<figure class="ArticleFigure_content__ueJhz ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_outdentDesktop__ijbiK ArticleFigure_outdent__tkMFK" role="group" data-component="ArticleFigure" aria-labelledby="102706190" data-uri="coremedia://imageproxy/102706190"<img alt="A thick storm cloud at Gantheaume Point in BRoome" class="Image_image__5tFYM image_contentImage__9bwU6" srcset="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/c7fa12684112417048afcde9d685a19e?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=538&amp;cropW=717&amp;xPos=780&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=647 543w, https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/c7fa12684112417048afcde9d685a19e?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=538&amp;cropW=807&amp;xPos=726&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=575" src="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/c7fa12684112417048afcde9d685a19e?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=538&amp;cropW=807&amp;xPos=726&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=575" loading="lazy" data-component="Image" style="--ratio-width:3;--ratio-height:2" data-lazy="true"<div class="ArticleFigcaption_desktopCaption__HYT8t"<figcaption class="Typography_base__sj2RP ArticleFigcaption_figcaption__tVy6G ArticleFigcaption_desktopFigcaption__LDNnU Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile20___U7Vr Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" id="102706190" data-component="ArticleFigure__figcaption" <!-- --In the 1960s the US used 'cloud seeding' to try to stop hurricanes<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP ArticleFigcaption_citation__5osFt Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" data-component="Byline"<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile20___U7Vr Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" data-component="Text"(<spanSupplied: Shahni Main</span)</span</span</figcaption</div<div class="ArticleFigcaption_caption__PDo_T"<button class="Button_btn___qFSk ArticleFigcaption_button__xUfr_ Button_filled__Z0XIL Button_uppercase__u_om3 Button_hasIcon__G3VLB Button_iconOnly__q0bR0" aria-label="Show caption" data-component="Button" aria-expanded="false" type="button"<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-component="Info" class="icon_icon__9kCSO icon_size24__GkyQ9"<circle cx="12" cy="12" r="9" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2"</circle<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="M12 7v2m0 2v6"</path</svg</button</div</figure<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Instead, researchers are exploring two new options.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Cyclones need hot sea surfaces to form. If we could cool the surface – such as by piping chilled water from depths below 200 metres – we could prevent the cyclone from ever forming.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"The problem is it's expensive. Norwegian cyclone-busting startup OceanTherm estimates it would cost about A$750 million to develop the technology, and another $105 million every year to keep it going.</p<aside class="ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_floatRight__nfR_t RelatedCard_relatedCard__ny1jQ" data-component="RelatedCard" data-uri="coremedia://article/102706150"<div data-component="CardBox" class="CardBox_padding__wBj1R"<a class="Link_link__5eL5m ScreenReaderOnly_srLinkHint__OysWz Link_showVisited__C1Fea Link_showFocus__ALyv2" href="https://www.abc.net.au/emergency/what-you-need-in-your-cyclone-emergency-kit/102612154" data-component="Link"<h3 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B CardHeading_cardHeading__FpsU_ RelatedCard_heading__UoYXS Typography_sizeMobile18__eJCIB Typography_sizeDesktop20___6qCS Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop24__Fh_y5 Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="CardHeading"<span class="KeyboardFocus_keyboardFocus__NLJda" data-component="KeyboardFocus"What you need in your cyclone emergency kit</span</h3<div class="CardLayout_flex__QnHKw CardLayout_mobileColumn__cTGc9 CardLayout_tabletColumn__8f7vO CardLayout_desktopColumn__JY3rV" data-component="CardLayout"<div class="CardLayout_content__zgsBr"<p class="Typography_base__sj2RP RelatedCard_synopsis__Z1uUh Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_bold__FqafP Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx" data-component="Typography"Not sure what you should have in your cyclone emergency kit? Check out our comprehensive list.</p</div<div class="CardLayout_imageContainer__wJ8ol CardLayout_mobileImageTop__uk0G9 CardLayout_tabletImageTop__BxHfE CardLayout_desktopImageTop__j7Nhk"<div class="ContentImage_ratio__0yYeG"<div class="AspectRatio_container__FC_XH" style="--aspect-ratio:1.7777777777777777" data-component="AspectRatioContainer"<img alt="A whole bunch of stuff to use in an emergency." class="Image_image__5tFYM ContentImage_image__DQ_cq" src="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/b5c6e6ec80751629594b6a3c7182e271?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=816&amp;cropW=1451&amp;xPos=0&amp;yPos=75&amp;width=862&amp;height=485" loading="lazy" data-component="Image" data-lazy="true"</div</div</div</div<span class="RelatedCard_moreLink__4V2M9"<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP Typography_sizeMobile14__u7TGe Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_bold__FqafP Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx" data-component="Typography"Read more</span<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-component="ArrowRight" class="icon_icon__9kCSO RelatedCard_icon__WB2_P icon_size20__HIjI5" aria-hidden="true"<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="m13 19 7-7-7-7"</path<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="M20 12H3"</path</svg</span</a</div</aside<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"And worse, cooling one area of the sea does nothing to stop cyclones from forming elsewhere. Models suggest ocean cooling will, at best, have only a limited dampening effect on cyclones.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"There's a more likely option – aerosol injection. Scientists already know that dust blown from the Sahara into the Atlantic reduces cyclone formation. We could use planes or drones to inject hygroscopic (water-attracting) particles into the lower atmosphere, where they would reflect and scatter sunlight and trigger rainfall and energy release.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"This method has a stronger scientific pedigree, given it already occurs naturally. But we don't know what side-effects it would have and we still aren't sure what happens to energy redistributed by the intervention.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Other research has found aerosols could reduce cyclone intensity while boosting rainfall on the rotating outer edges of cyclones. More intense rain could still cause substantial damage.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"As you'd expect, it's easier and more effective to intervene early in a cyclone's life, before too much energy builds up. Making the call to try to stop a cyclone means taking decisions early. That's a challenge, because cyclones can become stronger faster in a hotter world.</p<figure class="ArticleFigure_content__ueJhz ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_outdentDesktop__ijbiK ArticleFigure_outdent__tkMFK" role="group" data-component="ArticleFigure" aria-labelledby="102706342" data-uri="coremedia://imageproxy/102706342"<img alt="Global sea surface temperature anomalies on 18th July show warmer than normal ocean temperatures" class="Image_image__5tFYM image_contentImage__9bwU6" sizes="(max-width: 543px) 543px," srcset="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/f4ae2b05a3af7597f6879a22f7a91b35?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=746&amp;cropW=995&amp;xPos=117&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=647 543w, https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/f4ae2b05a3af7597f6879a22f7a91b35?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=746&amp;cropW=1119&amp;xPos=55&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=575" src="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/f4ae2b05a3af7597f6879a22f7a91b35?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=746&amp;cropW=1119&amp;xPos=55&amp;yPos=0&amp;width=862&amp;height=575" loading="lazy" data-component="Image" style="--ratio-width:3;--ratio-height:2" data-lazy="true"<div class="ArticleFigcaption_desktopCaption__HYT8t"<figcaption class="Typography_base__sj2RP ArticleFigcaption_figcaption__tVy6G ArticleFigcaption_desktopFigcaption__LDNnU Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile20___U7Vr Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" id="102706342" data-component="ArticleFigure__figcaption" <!-- --Global sea surface temperatures have risen across much of the globe, including near Australia.&nbsp;<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP ArticleFigcaption_citation__5osFt Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" data-component="Byline"<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile20___U7Vr Typography_regular__WeIG6 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_letterSpacedSm__V8kil" data-component="Text"(<spanSupplied: NOAA</span)</span</span</figcaption</div<div class="ArticleFigcaption_caption__PDo_T"<button class="Button_btn___qFSk ArticleFigcaption_button__xUfr_ Button_filled__Z0XIL Button_uppercase__u_om3 Button_hasIcon__G3VLB Button_iconOnly__q0bR0" aria-label="Show caption" data-component="Button" aria-expanded="false" type="button"<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-component="Info" class="icon_icon__9kCSO icon_size24__GkyQ9"<circle cx="12" cy="12" r="9" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2"</circle<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="M12 7v2m0 2v6"</path</svg</button</div</figure<h2 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B Typography_sizeMobile20__NUDn4 Typography_sizeDesktop32__LR_G6 Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop40__BuoRf Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="Heading"Difficult politics, difficult policy</h2<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Cyclone control missions might conjure up the image of Hollywood action heroes off to save the world.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Unfortunately, it's more complicated than that.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Let's say the Philippine government spots a extremely dangerous cyclone forming and decides to disrupt it. But the heat doesn't magically go away. It just moves. Suddenly, another storm reappears, heading straight for China, a country you have a testy relationship with, and who may blame you for weather manipulation.</p<aside class="ContentAlignment_marginBottom__4H_6E ContentAlignment_overflowAuto__c1_IL ContentAlignment_floatRight__nfR_t RelatedCard_relatedCard__ny1jQ" data-component="RelatedCard" data-uri="coremedia://article/102693258"<div data-component="CardBox" class="CardBox_padding__wBj1R"<a class="Link_link__5eL5m ScreenReaderOnly_srLinkHint__OysWz Link_showVisited__C1Fea Link_showFocus__ALyv2" href="/news/2023-08-03/china-hit-with-worst-flooding-in-over-a-decade/102681350" data-component="Link"<h3 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B CardHeading_cardHeading__FpsU_ RelatedCard_heading__UoYXS Typography_sizeMobile18__eJCIB Typography_sizeDesktop20___6qCS Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop24__Fh_y5 Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="CardHeading"<span class="KeyboardFocus_keyboardFocus__NLJda" data-component="KeyboardFocus"China hit by worst storms in a decade</span</h3<div class="CardLayout_flex__QnHKw CardLayout_mobileColumn__cTGc9 CardLayout_tabletColumn__8f7vO CardLayout_desktopColumn__JY3rV" data-component="CardLayout"<div class="CardLayout_content__zgsBr"<p class="Typography_base__sj2RP RelatedCard_synopsis__Z1uUh Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_bold__FqafP Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx" data-component="Typography"Typhoon Doksuri has wreaked havoc in northern China, bringing floods that have displaced thousands of people.</p</div<div class="CardLayout_imageContainer__wJ8ol CardLayout_mobileImageTop__uk0G9 CardLayout_tabletImageTop__BxHfE CardLayout_desktopImageTop__j7Nhk"<div class="ContentImage_ratio__0yYeG"<div class="AspectRatio_container__FC_XH" style="--aspect-ratio:1.7777777777777777" data-component="AspectRatioContainer"<img alt="Miaofengshan China floods_Typhoon (1)" class="Image_image__5tFYM ContentImage_image__DQ_cq" src="https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/a2705d27fb44359092500a5b1bceedf5?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize&amp;cropH=2813&amp;cropW=5000&amp;xPos=0&amp;yPos=260&amp;width=862&amp;height=485" loading="lazy" data-component="Image" data-lazy="true"</div</div</div</div<span class="RelatedCard_moreLink__4V2M9"<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP Typography_sizeMobile14__u7TGe Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_bold__FqafP Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx" data-component="Typography"Read more</span<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-component="ArrowRight" class="icon_icon__9kCSO RelatedCard_icon__WB2_P icon_size20__HIjI5" aria-hidden="true"<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="m13 19 7-7-7-7"</path<path stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" d="M20 12H3"</path</svg</span</a</div</aside<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Far-fetched? Not at all. When Cuban dictator Fidel Castro heard of Project STORMFURY, he feared it was an attempt to turn the weather into a weapon.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Only three years ago, China's neighbours sounded the alarm about the Middle Kingdom's plans to reroute an atmospheric "sky river" to dry northern regions. This, according to nations like India, could take water away from their rivers.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"So who would decide how or when to snuff out a cyclone? How would they decide? Should private companies be allowed to run their own field tests or should these large-scale interventions be government-only? Who would be responsible for any side-effects?</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"There are more thorny questions. If cyclone control is perfected, what would stop a country trying to redirect cyclones towards a rival? Could cyclone technologies be misused, following similar fears with large-scale geoengineering? Most importantly, are these technological risks worth the potentially reduced risks of cyclones?</p<h2 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B Typography_sizeMobile20__NUDn4 Typography_sizeDesktop32__LR_G6 Typography_lineHeightMobile24__crkfh Typography_lineHeightDesktop40__BuoRf Typography_marginBottomMobileSmall__6wx7m Typography_marginBottomDesktopSmall__CboX4 Typography_black__9qnZ1 Typography_colourInherit__dfnUx Typography_normalise__u5o1s" data-component="Heading"What's next?</h2<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"We'll need to find answers for questions like these. As cyclones get stronger, we will urgently need new institutions to help tackle scientific uncertainties, develop monitoring capabilities and find ways of making collaborative decisions at speed. That won't be easy – most international agreements move slowly, and most don't meet their intended goals.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"Technologies like particle injection are promising, but not ready for deployment. As the technology matures, so should our institutions. It's why we're researching the science and policy of these interventions. We must hash out how and when to use technologies like these – before we need to respond urgently.</p<p class="paragraph_paragraph___QITb"<strongAaron Tang is a PhD scholar in climate governance at Australian national University.&nbsp;Jack W Miller is a research assistant at ANU. Mark Howden is director of the ANU Institute for Climate, energy and Disaster Solutions at ANU, Roslyn Prinsley is head of Disaster Solutions at ANU&nbsp;and Thao Linh Tran is a Research Fellow at ANU.&nbsp;This piece first appeared on <a class="Link_link__5eL5m ScreenReaderOnly_srLinkHint__OysWz Link_showVisited__C1Fea Link_showFocus__ALyv2" href="https://theconversation.com/in-the-future-we-could-snuff-out-cyclones-but-weather-control-comes-with-new-risks-210788" data-component="Link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"The Conversation</a.</strong</p</div</div<div class="ArticleWeb_publishedDate__Z_2gs" data-component="Dateline"<span class="Typography_base__sj2RP Typography_sizeMobile12__w_FPC data-uri="coremedia://article/102649074"<div class="CardLayout_flex__QnHKw" data-component="CardLayout"<div class="CardLayout_content__zgsBr"<h3 class="Typography_base__sj2RP Heading_heading__VGa5B researchers are exploring two new options."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"Cyclones need hot sea surfaces to form. If we could cool the surface – such as by piping chilled water from depths below 200 metres – we could prevent the cyclone from ever forming."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"The problem is it's expensive. Norwegian cyclone-busting startup OceanTherm estimates it would cost about A$750 million to develop the technology, and another $105 million every year to keep it going."}]},{"type":"embed","key":"Article","props":{"linkTo":"https://www.abc.net.au/emergency/what-you-need-in-your-cyclone-emergency-kit/102612154","title":"What you need in your cyclone emergency kit","synopsis":"Not sure what you should have in your cyclone emergency kit? Check out our comprehensive list.","altText":"A whole bunch of stuff to use in an emergency.","thumbnail":{"url":"https://live-production.wcms.abc-cdn.net.au/b5c6e6ec80751629594b6a3c7182e271?impolicy=wcms_crop_resize\u0026cropH=816\u0026cropW=1451\u0026xPos=0\u0026yPos=75\u0026width=862\u0026height=485"},"viewType":"relatedstory","contentURI":"coremedia://article/102706150"},"children":[]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"And worse, cooling one area of the sea does nothing to stop cyclones from forming elsewhere. Models suggest ocean cooling will, at best, have only a limited dampening effect on cyclones."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"There's a more likely option – aerosol injection. Scientists already know that dust blown from the Sahara into the Atlantic reduces cyclone formation. We could use planes or drones to inject hygroscopic (water-attracting) particles into the lower atmosphere, where they would reflect and scatter sunlight and trigger rainfall and energy release."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"This method has a stronger scientific pedigree, given it already occurs naturally. But we don't know what side-effects it would have and we still aren't sure what happens to energy redistributed by the intervention."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"Other research has found aerosols could reduce cyclone intensity while boosting rainfall on the rotating outer edges of cyclones. More intense rain could still cause substantial damage."}]},{"type":"tagname","key":"p","props":{},"children":[{"type":"text","content":"As you'd expect, it's easier and more effective to intervene early in a cyclone's life, before too much energy builds up.
